Dispute over the Transfer of Ownership of the Daguangming Shoe Store - Creditors Unable to Recover Debts - Wang Youcai and Others Accused of Fraud

The Daguangming Shoe Store at 216 Guangxi Road, owned by Wang Youcai from Zhenjiang, has accumulated a significant amount of debt for goods. When creditors demanded payment, Wang repeatedly issued postdated checks as a delaying tactic. Xu Youchun, Xu Hengfu, Cai Xiangsheng, Huang Wushi, and others filed lawsuits in the First Special District Local Court one after another because they could not get the money when the checks matured, and they requested the seizure of the shoe store. Last week, the court dispatched personnel to seal the store, but they still could not obtain the money. The creditors suspected that Wang and others were committing fraud together and requested that the court investigate and prosecute them according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court held a hearing. Only Xu Youchun appeared as the plaintiff, stating that the Daguangming Shoe Store owed him more than 2,060 yuan for goods. After filing a lawsuit with the civil court, the defendant, Wang Youcai, hired lawyer Huang Xiubo to publish a notice calling for a transfer of ownership and to represent him in the liquidation. At that time, Xu Youchun entrusted a lawyer to send a letter to Huang Xiubo, expressing his objection, but Huang ignored it. When he obtained a court order and went to seize the store, Lu Shaoshan suddenly appeared to prevent it, claiming that he had taken over the store. This was clearly a case of joint fraud. The defendant, Huang Xiubo, filed a countersuit against the plaintiff, accusing him of false accusation. Judge Zhan adjourned the hearing to a later date because three other plaintiffs, including Xu Hengfu, had not appeared in court.

Xu Eying's Marriage Dissolution Case – Unilateral Argument Concluded

Xu Eying, a 21-year-old woman from Suzhou, whose original surname was Sun and whose father, Sun Kejian, was a doctor, went with her family to Hankou in 1932, where her father ran his business and they lived at 5 Eryi Street in Hankou. In November of that year, her mother arranged for her to change her surname to that of her maternal family, and Chai Hailou acted as a matchmaker, betrothing her to Zhu Qingxi, a young man from the same hometown and the son of her mother's close friend. At the time of the engagement, Zhu's mother had already passed away, but the marriage had been agreed upon by Zhu's mother during her lifetime. The groom's family sent betrothal gifts and jewelry to the bride's family to formalize the engagement. Now, Sun Eying believes that this marriage was arranged by her mother in her early years without her consent, which is a matter of lifelong happiness. Therefore, she asked the groom's family to dissolve the engagement, but the conditions were not right, and the matter could not be resolved. The woman currently lives in Hankou, while Zhu lives at 3 Yongqing Lane, Juji Da Road, in the French Concession of Shanghai. According to the civil procedure law, based on the principle of jurisdiction over the defendant's place of residence, she first filed a petition with the Second Special Court to mediate the dissolution of the engagement, but it was unsuccessful. Therefore, she hired lawyer Wang Shijia to represent her and formally filed a lawsuit against Zhu in the Special Court, requesting a judgment confirming the invalidity of the engagement. After repeated summonses, the defendant had moved and could not be reached. The plaintiff requested a public notice, which was approved. Yesterday, after the expiration of the public notice period, Judge Li Liang heard the case in the Civil Court No. 7. The defendant still did not appear. The plaintiff, Xu Eying, was represented by lawyer Wang Shizong, who stated the grounds for the lawsuit and the purpose of the request for judgment. The court examined the evidence and letters submitted by the plaintiff. Afterwards, the court allowed the plaintiff to present her argument unilaterally and announced the conclusion of the hearing, scheduling the judgment for 3:00 PM on the 31st.

Coal Industry Association Standardizes Coal Market Prices - To Be Implemented from the First Day of Next Month

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association, in order to standardize coal market prices, convened a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members and evaluation committee members at 2:00 PM yesterday. Over twenty people were present, including Bao Zhexian, Chen Weibin, Yang Runsheng, and Chen Yushu. Chairman Mao Chunpu discussed and evaluated coal market prices and the proposal that the industry should uniformly comply. The following was resolved: (1) To implement the standardization starting November 1st. (2) To submit the price list to the Bureau of Social Affairs for record-keeping before printing and distributing it to members. (3) To publish the notice in newspapers, informing the industry to comply. The Association's notice reads: "We hereby inform you that in order to eliminate market price disorder and avoid sales disputes, the Association has evaluated and set fair prices for various types of coal in order to achieve standardization. In accordance with industry regulations, a detailed coal price list has been prepared and submitted to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for record-keeping. The joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members has decided to implement it on November 1st. Therefore, a copy of the evaluated coal price list will be printed and distributed to member firms, and a public notice will be published in newspapers. We hope everyone will be informed and comply accordingly. Any violations will be punished according to the legally prescribed industry regulations. Do not neglect this. Furthermore, member and non-member firms who need the coal price list should send a letter to the Association to obtain it."

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor, I have read the "Dispute over a Student Being Driven Away and Breaking His Leg" in the news column of this newspaper on the 28th of this month. The content is inconsistent with the facts. The child did not enter the platform without permission and tried to climb the coal platform. When he saw someone, he panicked and ran away, lost his balance, and was injured. The stationmaster and the police reported the incident at the time. I am afraid that the rumor will be passed on, causing the truth to be lost and harming my reputation. I respectfully request that you correct the mistake. Sincerely, Hua Guohun, October 29, 1935.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Xiao Bai)

"Patience" is acceptable, but do not take the road of "submission."

In the turbulent modern era of the twentieth century, we certainly cannot endure in the style of "drying ourselves while sleeping." However, we must not imitate Jesus by offering the left cheek after being slapped on the right, because that is not patience; that is an expression of extreme weakness, that is, a complete act of submission.

"Patience" must have its proper limits; it has a temporal and spatial nature. In other words, patience is by no means a passive invasion. Rather, it is a deeper understanding, followed by temporary endurance. But by no means should patience erode your inherent perseverance.

The End of a Wrong Path

— Lan Shan

On this day, a young man with elegant clothes and a haggard face was added to cell number so-and-so. Because his demeanor was unlike that of a vicious thief, all the prisoners in the cell gave him a surprised look, as if welcoming this fair-skinned new comrade. The young man dragged his student's shackles, changed into prison clothes, and his facial expressions were constantly changing, sometimes ashamed, sometimes alarmed, sometimes resentful, and finally he slumped down.

The cell was not very bright, and the air had a strange smell, which made him very uncomfortable. However, when he thought about the fact that he had to live here for two years, he had to make the best of it. At this time, an older prisoner came over to greet him:

"Hey! Brother, what rule did you break to get sent in here? You don't seem like one of us! Can you tell us what happened?"

When the young man heard this question, tears welled up in his eyes, and he choked out the words:

"Alas! It's my fault, I took the wrong path. I deserve it, I deserve it! I used to manage accounts at a certain bank, and life was very comfortable. I accidentally went to a brothel with some friends and met a beautiful girl. After that, I was completely infatuated. I couldn't go a day without seeing her. My limited money couldn't win her favor. She was a famous prostitute. I was truly too blinded. Last month, I stole more than 13,000 yuan from the bank and hid in her courtyard. I only enjoyed myself for eight days before I was discovered. More than 12,000 yuan of the stolen money was recovered by the bank, and I was sentenced to two years in prison. That's why I'm here. It's my fault, I deserve it. I just feel sorry for my old mother at home, I don't know how heartbroken she will be..."

Everyone fell silent.

Female Guide

— Bing Ding

The day before yesterday, I went to a friend's club to chat, but everyone felt very bored. My friend said: "Recently, someone started a business that can meet the needs of lonely people. Let's try it." As he spoke, he got up to make a phone call.

Not long after, a robust woman suddenly came into our club, smiling broadly, and sat down, asking us: "Do you like to travel? Shop? Sightsee? Tour scenic spots? Please tell me what kind of guidance you need." She was experienced and serious, and she spoke to us in the local dialect without any shyness or frivolousness.

We didn't want to sightsee or shop, but because we were curious, we talked to her about random things. Only then did we learn that the mission of the guiding staff was: (1) To accompany people who are new to Shanghai and unfamiliar with the area on tours. (2) To assist Chinese and foreign visitors passing through Shanghai who want to see the sights by providing experienced Shanghai guides. (3) To accompany guests on tours of the many scenic spots and historical sites in Shanghai, a major metropolis in East Asia. Oh! We understood that they were all experienced hands.

We thought that people who have lived in the city for a long time probably know the general outline of the city and don't need to ask for advice. However, the dark side of the city is really not very clear. This is where we need to consult the old hands, but I don't know if they would be willing to guide us?

We have legal counsel to protect our lives and property; we have female guides for entertainment. It's really fun to live in Shanghai.

Nanhu Melody

— Shu Fan

The water wind rustles the trees, such a peaceful lake has evening tides!

The white-haired old mother cherishes her strength, and must still carry passengers across the lake bridge.

My family's gentle oars are worth gold, the lake's reeds are my cold quilt.

I have anchored everywhere in the thirty-six bays, who wants to hear about my happy times?

The water products of Nanhu are very cheap, I peel them for the old restaurant until my fingers are sore.

I am used to seeing the water caltrop flowers bloom and wither, I am too unlucky to eat green caltrop!

I am most afraid of the sound of trees when the boat is moored, I cover myself with a bird awning and a straw raincoat.

All night long, the clear coldness and the white shadow of the waves, my sisters and I are Chang'e!

Repentance Convent

No need for prayer cushions or jade chimes, the old nun's work is in autumn silkworms.

Unprovoked, I extinguished the lotus lantern light, a handful of youthful silk is the beautiful little convent.

Autumn Rain Meeting in Smoke and Rain Tower

The leaning tower stands distinctly, the wooden boat and reed canopy float crampedly.

With tired feet, I listen to the heavens and am startled for half a lifetime!

The cold lake extinguishes the candle past mid-autumn; my teeth are tired of the old red shrimp,

How can my lungs bear the white dew? Thanks to the misty smoke for concealing the moon's outline,

The pure light is generously bestowed upon my old Confucian head!

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty: Struggling to Live, Watching a Cherished Grandson, Crying in Despair, Recalling the Famine Years, Planting Wheat Brings Disaster

Yueying said: "Later, he took my father to the army. In the fortress, there was another person who planted a lot of wheat, and he was also taken away. My grandmother, my mother, and I saw them taking people away and followed behind. Those soldiers first used their guns to stop us and prevent us from going. Later, the military officer said, 'It's okay to let them go and see,' so he let us go. People in the fortress were worried and followed us too. Unexpectedly, they took people away and, without asking many questions, they hung my father and the person from the fortress who went with him?" Mrs. Zhou said: "What do you mean by 'hanging'?" Yueying said: "It means tying people's hands and feet together and hanging them from the roof beam." Mrs. Zhou said, "So, the person is suspended in the air. How can they bear that?" Yueying said: "That's still good. Usually when they hang people, they use leather whips to beat them." Mrs. Zhou said: "Since you know about this, is it common in Gansu to whip people with leather whips?" Yueying said: "The county magistrate often tortures people to collect taxes." Mrs. Zhou said: "Then you don't take this kind of torture seriously anymore." Yueying was distressed. "Others just watch, but we, as family members, are terrified to see them hanging like that. We can only kneel on the ground and beg the military officer for mercy. They are truly iron-hearted. After they hung my father up, they only left four soldiers to guard the empty house. We knelt and begged, but they didn't hear or see us. It just so happened that two walls of the room where they were torturing my father collapsed, so we could see very clearly from the outside. My father's hands and feet were tied together behind his back, and his face was facing down. He was hanging on the beam like a thing being hung. At first, my father endured it without making a sound, but later he shouted for the commander to have mercy and save him. Then, he couldn't even shout for mercy, and his face changed from red to gray. All he could do was groan! My family, and the family of the person from the fortress who came with us, all knelt in the courtyard outside the house, crying together." (352)

御香縹緲錄

— Translated by Qin Shouou from the original work of Princess Der Ling of Qing Dynasty

From where I stood near the Empress Dowager, I clearly saw her shoulders suddenly heave after listening to Li Lianying's words, almost as if she was about to jump up from her seat. I couldn't help but be startled as well. Although I knew that late autumn was not the season for magnolia blossoms, I did not understand what constituted an auspicious or ominous sign, so the Empress Dowager's great shock left me rather puzzled. Thus, I held my breath and listened attentively.

"What? Have those magnolia trees bloomed again?" the Empress Dowager asked with an uncharacteristic air of panic. "Quickly tell me the details! Tell me now! Quickly!"

"Reporting to the Empress Dowager! This humble servant would never dare to lie! It is all true! Just now, a gardener reported that there is indeed a magnolia flower that has bloomed..."

"Only one flower?"

"Yes, Your Majesty! It is said that it is on the oldest magnolia tree in the garden, and today a single, perfectly formed flower is in full bloom. This is truly a rare occurrence in ancient times, and there is no need for further explanation; everyone knows it is a sign of great fortune and auspiciousness!"

Li Lianying kept chanting "fortune" and "auspiciousness," but our Empress Dowager was already stunned. Her face instantly turned ashen, and she seemed to want to say something, but only her lips were seen opening and closing. After a moment, a sound was heard coming out. In those four or five minutes, her age seemed to have suddenly increased by ten years, like a thermometer rising. We could also clearly see that the five fingers of one hand she had pressed on her chest were trembling excessively due to the shock. However, aside from Li Lianying, none of us who served her understood the reason, let alone how to comfort her. We could only let her silently worry about the great disaster she believed was about to befall her. (448)

"Big Chiming Clock" Without a Clock

— Yi Yi Guan Zhu

"Big Chiming Clock" is the name of a tram stop in the French Concession of Shanghai, located between "Zhengjia Wood Bridge" and "Jixiang Street." Anyone who has been to Shanghai knows it.

As for why it is called "Big Chiming Clock," I think few people pay attention. As far as I know, it is because the central police station of the French Concession is located there, and the police station used to have a "Big Chiming Clock" on top of it. Therefore, the place was named "Big Chiming Clock."

However, the central police station there has now been rebuilt into a nine-story building, and there is no clock on top. Yet the place is still called "Big Chiming Clock." I think that in the long run, it may become like "Stealing Chicken Bridge," "Eight Immortals Bridge," "Dongxin Bridge," "Xixin Bridge," and "Zhengjia Wood Bridge" – a name that doesn't match the reality, leaving people confused! I record this for future reference.

Small Recipe

Talking About Crabs

— Nangong Sheng

At this time, as early autumn arrives, the west wind begins to blow, the clear frost first falls, and maple leaves gradually turn red, it is the time when lake crabs are plump and full. Holding a crab claw and admiring chrysanthemums, peeling the shell and picking out the yolk, even an old diner's index finger moves. The crab stalls in the market are also becoming more and more prosperous. Crabs are an aquatic creature, delicious and rich in flavor, and they are produced in all seasons. However, the crabs in spring have not yet fully grown, and they are small and empty. Although they are plumper in summer, the season is short, and they are not very palatable. It is only when the mulberry leaves turn yellow and the west wind blows in late autumn that they become fat and large, with ample yolk and a fresh, rich flavor. In winter, the lake water freezes, and production is scarce, so the best time to eat crabs is now, in late autumn and early winter, when they are in season.

Crabs are divided into sand crabs and freshwater crabs. Sand crabs are produced in the sandy waters of rivers. Their taste is slightly salty and far inferior to freshwater crabs. Freshwater crabs are produced in freshwater, and their taste is sweet, rich, and delicious. They are the finest type of crab. They are produced in large quantities in the Jiangnan region, and the Yangcheng Lake in Zheng Yi is the most famous. Because the water of Yangcheng Lake is clear to the bottom, the crabs produced there are truly sweet freshwater crabs, and their taste is far superior to those produced elsewhere. Moreover, Yangcheng crabs have a unique characteristic: they have green backs, white bellies, golden claws, and red hairs, so they are called Golden Claw Yangcheng crabs. Besides Yangcheng crabs, crabs from Zhouzhuang and other places are also a type of freshwater crab. Although they are inferior to Yangcheng crabs, they are also a famous product. Sand crabs are produced in large quantities along the Yangtze River, but they are far inferior to Yangcheng Lake crabs.

The largest crabs seen in the market now are no bigger than a bowl. In the past, it was said that the largest crabs could grow to nine feet long and have white feet, called hundred-foot crabs, as recorded in the "Dongming Ji." During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, the Kingdom of Chunyuan presented a crab that was nine feet long, with a hundred claws, named the hundred-foot crab. There was also a crab that could carry a cart, which was even more magnificent than the hundred-foot crab. "The Ji Family's Book Collection" records a large crab from Haiyang that required a cart to carry, its size imaginable.

Crab is a general term. The female is commonly called "round navel" or "broad belt." The male is called "pointed navel" or "wave rake." According to "Guangya," "crab means 'kneeling'; the male is called 'wave rake,' the female 'broad belt.'" According to "Lu Kang's Crab Picture Record," there are twelve types of crabs in total. Kang ordered craftsmen to draw crab pictures, and there were twelve types: "one is 'youbang'," "two is 'paddle'," "three is 'sword holder'," "four is 'pengwei'," "five is 'jiepu'," "six is 'sand dog'," "seven is 'wangchao'," "eight is 'yiwang'," "nine is 'shiyan'," "ten is 'fengjiang'," "eleven is 'luhu'," and "twelve is 'pengqi'." Of these twelve crab names, only the twelfth, "pengqi," still exists today; the others have not been heard of.

There were also many strange stories about crabs in the past. The strangest is that they can drive away sore ghosts, as recorded in "Dream Stream Essays." There are no crabs in Guanzhong. Someone occasionally obtained a crab, feared its appearance, and thought it was a monster. When someone had sores, they would borrow it to guard the door, and often the sores would heal. Not only did people not recognize it, but ghosts also did not recognize it. This is truly an unheard-of strange thing. However, in the past, some people believed this to be true because they often thought that sores were caused by sore ghosts. Now that science is developed, everyone knows that sores are caused by microorganisms, and there is no such thing as ghosts. No one can believe that crabs can cure sores.

Although crab is a delicacy that everyone likes to eat, it is extremely cold in nature, and the crab shell is also dry. Eating too much is not beneficial. Therefore, when cooking crabs, perilla and ginger are often cooked together to dispel the coldness of the crab. Eating crab and persimmon together can be fatal, commonly known as "crab crawling intestines." In fact, both persimmon and crab are extremely cold. Eating them together at the same time can naturally cause illness, and it is not true that the crab in the stomach will actively crawl up the intestines!

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders Textbooks Must Be Reviewed First

Then Sent to the Ministry of Interior for Registration

(Nanjing, 29th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education instructs various departments that Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Copyright Law stipulates that the Ministry of Interior shall not register textbooks that should be reviewed by the Da Xue Yuan (National Academy) according to laws and regulations before they have been reviewed by the Da Xue Yuan. Therefore, textbooks used in schools at all levels should not be sent to the Ministry of Interior for registration before they have been reviewed by the former Da Xue Yuan or this Ministry. Recently, it has been discovered that many bookstores directly send textbooks that should be reviewed by this Ministry to the Ministry of Interior for registration, attempting to evade the review procedures, which is highly inappropriate. Hereafter, bookstores should send textbooks used in schools at all levels to this Ministry for review in accordance with the law and shall not attempt to evade the review, causing disorder in the procedures. The relevant departments are instructed to direct all bookstores to strictly comply.

Jiangsu Teachers' Union Appeals for Children in Disaster Areas

The Jiangsu Provincial Elementary School Teachers' Union issued an appeal to all sectors of society regarding the children in disaster areas, stating: "China is afflicted by natural disasters, and calamities occur frequently. Last year's severe drought has barely subsided, and the wounds have not yet healed. Now, the severity of this autumn's floods is no less than that of the floods in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), and the scope is even wider. Almost all three major rivers in the country have experienced problems simultaneously, and the Yangtze and Yellow River basins have been the most severely affected. Due to the heavy rainfall in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and the flooding of the Xiang River, the areas north of Hubei have largely become a watery land. Due to the torrential rains of the Yi and Luo Rivers, the Yellow River breached its banks in Henan and Shandong, and the disaster spread to northern Jiangsu. In total, the disaster has affected a vast area spanning sixteen provinces, and the number of victims is as high as twenty-five million. Some entire villages have been submerged, some entire counties have sunk, some have left their parents and wives and fled in all directions, and some have been unable to escape and have been buried in the bellies of fish. There are also families, old and young, who could not bear to be separated and tied themselves together with ropes and died together in the disaster. It can be said to be tragic. It is human nature to love life and hate death. If we were in their place, how could we not feel sorrow? The misfortune of children in disaster areas is particularly heartbreaking. Children are the lifeblood of the nation, rich in youth and with unlimited potential. However, due to their insufficient physical strength, they are unable to resist the invasion of floods. The number of those who drowned because they were unable to escape or who sacrificed themselves due to exhaustion during the escape is alarming. Those who have died are gone, and those who have survived are unable to attend school because schools have been closed, they have no place to live because houses have collapsed, they are separated from their parents and elders and have no one to rely on, or they are suffering from hunger and cold due to lack of food and clothing, or they are groaning in bed due to disease. After a major disaster, there is bound to be a major epidemic. Those who do not die from the water will die from disease. What could be more tragic than this? Everyone loves their children. The fathers and brothers in the disaster areas are not callous enough to sit idly by and watch their beloved children live in a state of displacement and hardship without thinking of ways to help. However, after surviving the disaster, their minds and bodies are exhausted. Although they have a compassionate heart for children, they lack the means to provide universal relief. We hope that people from all walks of life at home and abroad will follow the teachings of the ancient Confucian scholars who mourned for all mankind. If you close your eyes and think quietly, the plight of children in disaster areas will appear before your eyes. You should also have the Buddhist heart of saving all living beings, providing food, clothing, or money to help these victims and lead them to the shore of safety. First, provide life relief to prevent them from freezing and starving, and then provide educational relief to prevent them from dropping out of school. This is not only the fortune of children in disaster areas, but also the future of China depends on it. Furthermore, this year happens to be China's Children's Year. The government and the people are working together to improve the well-being of children across the country. The most unfortunate children in China at present are those in disaster areas. Therefore, the most urgent task of Children's Year is to seek happiness for children in disaster areas. It would not be an exaggeration to say that the success or failure of rescuing children in disaster areas is the success or failure of China's implementation of Children's Year. May all our compatriots strive for it."

Jiangsu Boy Scouts Review Yangzhong Township Division Achieving Excellent Results

China Boy Scout General Association First Anniversary

Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters Notifies County Party Headquarters to Celebrate on November 1st Following the Procedures

The Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters issued a notice to the County Party Headquarters: "In accordance with the China Boy Scout General Association's letter Zhi Zi No. 1127, this year's November 1st is the first anniversary of the Association's establishment. Celebrations should be held to commemorate it. The celebration procedures have been formulated and are sent along with this letter. The Boy Scouts in each province, city, and county shall hold celebrations at 1 p.m. on that day. In addition to separate instructions, this letter is sent for your information. Please instruct the local Boy Scout troops or organizing agencies to comply accordingly." In accordance with this, in addition to separate instructions, this order is issued for compliance.

Celebration Procedures (Attached original text of the celebration procedures): 1. From November 1st of this year, the Boy Scouts in each province, city, and county shall hold a ceremony every year at 1 p.m. on that day to celebrate the anniversary of the establishment of the China Boy Scout General Association. 2. The celebration of the founding anniversary of the China Boy Scout General Association shall be led by the provincial, city, or county council (the provincial council leads the Boy Scouts of the provincial capital. 3. Provinces, cities, and counties that have not established councils may be convened by the provincial, county, or city party headquarters or education department/bureau to hold the ceremony with all local Boy Scouts. The procedure for the celebration meeting is tentatively set as follows: 1. Opening; 2. Playing music (firecrackers can also be set off at the same time); 3. Raising the flag; 4. Singing the Party song; 5. Paying the highest respect to the national party flag and the image of the Premier; 6. The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; 7. All Boy Scouts recite the oath; 8. The chairman reports; 9. A celebrity gives a speech on the meaning of Boy Scout education; 10. Cheers; 11. Singing the Boy Scout song; 12. Adjournment. 5. The venue for holding the celebration meeting should be an open-air square and the publicity should be expanded in advance so that the public can understand the meaning of the Boy Scouts and encourage the public's children to join the Boy Scout Red Fabric Society. 6. Slogans and drawings promoting Boy Scout education can be pasted around the celebration venue and nearby. 7. The celebration can be concluded with the Boy Scouts participating in activities beneficial to the local area. 8. The situation of the celebrations held in each province, city, and county should be notified by the responsible leading agency or submitted to the General Association for record. 9. These procedures shall be promulgated and implemented by the China Boy Scout General Association.

Overview of Recent Education in Hubei Province

Cheng Qibao, Director of the Education Department of Hubei Province, is determined to govern well. Since the last time he convened a meeting of domestic education experts in Hubei, he formulated an improvement plan based on the educational situation in the province for reference, and asked the experts to guide and determine the future direction of educational efforts. The following is a summary of the recent educational situation in the province after the summer of this year.

(A) Higher Education In addition to this year's 24th term of three government-funded students sent abroad (one to the United Kingdom to study fisheries, one to Austria to study police administration, and one to the United States to study agriculture), scholarship measures have been formulated for self-funded students studying abroad from the province to encourage them. The Education Department organized a review committee to review the documents submitted by the students and approved them. Scholarships will be provided from this year, and the Ministry of Education has been consulted and approved. There are six self-funded students studying in France and one self-funded student studying in the United States. The Ministry of Education has also revised the method of issuing tuition fees to government-funded students going abroad for the first time to enable students to concentrate on their studies and work hard. The first three months of government funding will be issued at the time of departure as stipulated. The government funding for the fourth, fifth, and sixth months will be remitted in advance in the early, mid, and late periods of the previous month. The government funding for the seventh, eighth, and ninth months will be remitted in advance in the early, mid, and late periods of the current month. (In the past, according to regulations, the fourth month's government funding had to be remitted together with the tuition fees for other government-funded students.) The government funding for the tenth month and thereafter will be remitted at the same time as the government funding for other government-funded students every month.

(B) Secondary Education In addition to holding education research conferences and competitions for secondary schools, teacher training schools, and various types of schools, and increasing the funding for assisting excellent private secondary schools this year, there are several plans for improving the teaching plans of secondary schools: (1) High schools should restore the elective system so that students can choose to study according to their interests. (2) Foreign language should be reduced in junior high schools to improve the level of Chinese and other subjects. (3) Teacher training school courses are numerous, and the time is often insufficient. The length of study should be extended by one year to allow students to receive sufficient training. (4) Teacher training schools have fewer teaching hours for common subjects than secondary schools. If the same textbooks are used, the time is insufficient. Textbooks should be compiled separately for application. (5) The plan to train high school graduates in teacher training schools for one year should be postponed until there is a shortage of teachers. (6-7) Omitted (8) Both physics and chemistry are subjects that study natural phenomena. Physics studies temporary phenomena, while chemistry studies permanent phenomena. Physics studies the shape of objects, while chemistry studies the quality of objects. Therefore, those who study the theory should start with physics first, identify its shape first, and then analyze its changes (characteristics). In the school system, chemistry is included in the second year and physics is included in the third year. This is originally upside down, and teaching is extremely difficult. It should be corrected immediately.

(C) Vocational Education The province has formulated an implementation plan for vocational education, which will be implemented starting this year. The general plan is to convert the Provincial Second Middle School into the Wuchang Commercial Vocational School, the Third Middle School into the Hanyang Industrial Vocational School, and add a Hubei Central Agricultural Vocational School. One junior agricultural vocational school is planned to be added in eastern Hubei, western Hubei, southern Hubei, and northern Hubei. The original vocational schools will be converted or add remedial classes that meet the needs. The vocational education funding will be increased by more than 86,000 yuan in the 24th year. After reducing two classes in each of the ordinary middle school, high school, and junior high school, the funding will be gradually increased according to the Ministry-set joint school funding standards.

(D) Elementary Education Because the province is vigorously implementing the Baojia system, in addition to instilling knowledge of rural organizations and self-defense and autonomy to rural children, the provincial government has stipulated that each county's Lianbao (joint guarantee) should establish elementary schools, implementing a system of integrating politics and education. Each county's Lianbao should establish one of the various types of schools (divided into primary elementary schools, simple elementary schools, short-term elementary schools, and mass schools) stipulated in the measures in the 24th year, and should be promoted year by year thereafter. If the province's Education Department implements the measures for county magistrates and district offices to bear considerable educational responsibility, then the province's education will not be difficult to popularize.

(E) Social Education The province has formulated the Hubei Province Literacy Education Program, which includes measures for the organization of mobilization agencies, the source of teachers, the implementation procedures, research and guidance funding, and local promotion assistance, which will be implemented in stages. Plans have also been made for the implementation of mass education in county and district units.

Shanghai County Implements Compulsory Literacy Education

The First Phase is Scheduled to Begin on December 1st; Two Phases are Conducted Each Year, Each Lasting Three Months

Shanghai County has a total population of more than 120,000, of whom more than 70,000 are illiterate. The county government has implemented compulsory literacy education in accordance with provincial orders. Preparations, surveys, and other work according to the predetermined procedures have been completed. The first phase is scheduled to begin on November 1st, with teachers and staff from public and private primary and secondary schools and civil education centers responsible for teaching. A total of 124 classes will be offered, each enrolling 50 students, and will graduate in three months. The county uses April to October as the busy farming season and November to April as the slack farming season, so literacy education is carried out during the slack farming season. Two phases are held each year, and it is planned to complete four phases in two years to complete the preliminary plan, it is said.

Nanjing Primary School Calligraphy Research Society Publishes Simplified Character Model

The Primary School Calligraphy Research Society at No. 1, Pingcang Lane, Gulou, Nanjing, has always been dedicated to researching and improving calligraphy teaching. This year, in view of the fact that simplified characters are a useful tool for popularizing education and that all sectors of society urgently need to learn them, the members, led by Mr. Sun Tongchuo, have printed a model based on the simplified character list announced by the Ministry of Education. The characters are accurate, the structure is rigorous, and the simplified character order announced by the Ministry of Education and teaching methods are attached. It is truly an indispensable book for all sectors of society. The whole book has forty-five pages, printed in fine quality newsprint, priced at one jiao, and sold at a 60% discount during the special offer period. It is reported that various government agencies and education bureaus have ordered in large quantities from the society to distribute to schools and subordinate agencies as models.

Little Men (79)

— Original by Ms. Olcott of the United States, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Nan En didn't have time to think of any embellishments, but Xiaomei had already poured out the whole story, making Tai Fei unable to find a place to hide, so he could only hide his face in the bowl of milk and bread. After the story was over, Mr. Pei's eyes went straight to his wife at the end of the long table, his eyes full of smiles, saying:

"Dear, this matter is about your part, so I don't want to interfere with it."

Mrs. Shu knew what he meant, but she now loved her little black sheep even more, because she had such courage, but on the outside she only put on the most solemn expression and said:

"Do you know why Nan En was brought here?"

With his mouth full of food, Tai Fei muttered to himself, "Just trick me."

"She is here to help me make you all little gentlemen. I think you have shown it, and some of you need this very much."

Speaking of this, Tai Fei hid his face in his bowl again, and dared not raise his head again, until Xiao Qiao said a word, which made everyone laugh, because he said in his slow tone, expressing surprise:

"How can she be able to, she herself is like a man!"

"That's exactly why she needs help like you do, I hope you give her a good example of etiquette."

"Does she want to make a little gentleman too?" Robert asked.

"She wants to too; doesn't she, Nan En?" Tao Mo asked Nan En.

Additional Notes:

1. The time, venue, and referee for each game will be announced in the newspaper every Wednesday.

2. The scheduled date must not be changed. If it is changed due to rain or unavoidable accidents, the make-up game will be arranged by this association.

3. If the weather is not good and the applicability of the venue is uncertain, the home team should consult with the away team to determine the venue one day before the game. If the date is changed due to the venue not being applicable, the home team should report to the secretary of the association and try to notify the referee.

4. For each game, the home team should be responsible for properly arranging the venue in advance (drawing lines, installing goal nets, preparing small flags for linesmen, and preparing the balls for the game, etc.), and not prepare at the last minute, so as not to hinder the game time.

5. The home team shall be responsible for maintaining order in the game. However, the away team should also fulfill its obligation to assist.

6. The report form for each game should be collected from the referee before the start of the game, filled out, and returned to the referee during the break after the first half.

French Professional Tennis Player Kochin-Eyde Will Come to Shanghai

Has Already Agreed to Matches Against Carnavaro and Aragui; Location Undecided, Either at the French Chamber of Commerce or the Shanghai Club

The news that the French professional tennis player Kochin-Eyde will come to Shanghai, which was a sensation for a while, has recently gradually faded. The reporter met with Qiu Feihai, a national player of our country, in Shanghai and Beijing the other day. According to Mr. Qiu, he recently received a telegram from Mr. Kochin, who is currently performing in Hong Kong and plans to take the Hoover President Liner north from Hong Kong on the 2nd of next month and arrive in Shanghai around the 4th. If time is not enough, he plans to take the French postal ship Zhen Nusha, which sails from Hong Kong on the 3rd, and arrive in Shanghai around the 6th. As for the opponents for the performances in Shanghai, he has agreed to matches against the local professional tennis player Carnavaro and the Philippine professional coach Aragui. The location will be at the French Chamber of Commerce or the Shanghai Tennis Club, it is said.

The content is very rich, and the pictures and text are systematic. Most of the photos are specially taken, which are exceptionally wonderful and different from others. The grand occasion of the Games is lively on paper, as if you are on the scene. The newspaper is being rushed to print and will be published soon. The price is six jiao. Pre-orders before the end of October will only cost half price, three jiao. Add two fen for postage in this city, and four fen for other cities. If you need to register, add eight fen. The number of pre-orders in this city and other cities will reach 10,000. The pre-order period is only for today and tomorrow. Out-of-town subscriptions are subject to the postmark. After publication, it will be sold at the original price. Schools and sports enthusiasts must subscribe quickly, it is said.

The Suzhou Football Disaster Relief Matches, initiated by the gentry of Wuxian County, were originally scheduled to be held in early this month. As for the date of the expedition, it remains to be discussed. Originally, it could be done at the end of the month, but since the Youyou Donghua teams will play in the West League this Sunday in Shenyuan, it is feared that it will be postponed to early next month, it is said.

Shanghai National Arts Museum Seeks Short-Term Members

The Shanghai National Arts Museum is the leading agency for national arts in the city. At this National Games, the city won the third place in the total scores of men's and women's national arts. The statistics are very satisfactory, which shows that the museum's daily guidance is effective. After the closing of the National Games, people in the community attach great importance to national arts and have written to the museum to specially add classes. It is now learned that the museum has specially added short-term membership classes to meet the needs of the community. The period is from November 1st to the end of February next year, a full four months. The total cost is five yuan. The subjects include Tai Chi, Shaolin, Xingyi, Bagua, Wrestling, Archery, etc. The museum has already started seeking members. Those who are interested in learning national arts can go to the main hall on Minkuo Road, Xinkaihe, or the special district office at Tianhou Palace on Beihenan Road to obtain the regulations and register, it is said.

Free Talk

On Eating Vegetarian

— Yao Mu

Following the great popularity of Buddhism, the trend of eating vegetarian has also become extremely popular. From uneducated village women to high-ranking officials, once they have converted to the Buddha, they naturally become vegetarians. Vegetarian restaurants have become a form of speculative business here, sprouting up like mushrooms after the rain in the sluggish market.

Needless to say, in the eyes of female and male Buddhist followers, eating vegetarian means not killing living beings, and not killing living beings is a meritorious deed. In fact, among the 400 million people in China, those who cultivate this merit, to put it mildly, number 200 million. Country people are almost all "natural" vegetarians. Ascetics who gnaw on grass roots and tree bark are becoming more and more numerous every day. How many ordinary farmers can afford to eat meat three or two times a year? The chickens and pigs they treat as their own lives are not raised to satisfy the appetites of others? Therefore, the saying "Why not eat meat porridge?" is still a "cool breeze" even in good years.

However, after the high-ranking officials and gentlemen are tired of eating shark fins and bird's nests to the point of being fat and sluggish, eating tofu and meditating on "Jade Tablet Zen," returning from extreme splendor to simplicity, is not bad, and is also a way to maintain health.

I have no affinity with Buddhism, but I sometimes like to eat vegetarian food. Many of my relatives and friends are vegetarians. When I was twelve or thirteen years old, because of two vegetarian cousins, I began to know the flavor of vegetarian food. The elder cousin was a poor widow without children. Remaining a widow and eating vegetarian food naturally go together easily. The second cousin was an unmarried woman nearly thirty years old. Because she suffered a serious illness, her parents made a vow before the Bodhisattva to practice asceticism with her hair uncut. At that time, they often stayed overnight at our house, accompanying my mother and sister. They were good at cooking vegetarian dishes. On festivals and birthdays, they personally cooked for us. Vegetarian duck and vegetarian ham were made to look and taste just like the real thing. The elder cousin lived under the oppression of usury and the bullying of her sisters-in-law. She would secretly shed tears and sigh, and her face would turn red if she spoke a few words to strangers. The second cousin was clever and good at serving others, but she was a bit narrow-minded, and always seemed to have a chest full of depression. But they both liked my sister and me very much. Among the family, only the two of us sisters could make them laugh. At that time, our family was in

a kind of unfortunate situation. Their attentiveness and thoughtfulness gave my sickly and melancholy mother a lot of comfort, and we also gained two older sisters and nanny-like companions. Their home was not far from ours. As soon as dusk fell and we had eaten dinner, we sisters would go to fetch them. We often shed tears because they refused, and only stopped crying when they agreed. When we crossed the small stone bridge along the river, carrying the new moon, and brushed through the ruined garden hidden by flowering branches, back to our home, our young and elegant hearts were filled with the joy of victory. We hurriedly picked a few jasmine flowers blooming in the dusk in the courtyard, and insisted on putting them on their heads, to express our gratitude. After they talked with my mother, they would tell us stories and riddles in the yard. We felt unbearable loneliness if we didn't see them for a day. Truly, among our relatives, they were the only ones who left the deepest impression on our childhood.

In the blink of an eye, more than ten years have passed. More and more relatives and friends are studying Buddhism and eating vegetarian food. However, in the year I entered middle school, the second cousin passed away, suffering from the lung disease that women often get. As for the elder cousin, I haven't seen her for several years. I heard that she is still surviving, even though she often vomits a basin full of blood, and is old and haggard like an old woman, she still has to borrow new debts to repay old debts, relying on her ten fingers to live out her twilight years as a widow, half-starved and half-fed. Although their tragic experiences are not the result of eating vegetarian food, when I talk about eating vegetarian food, I can't help but think of my cousins' tragic experiences.

In a large part of Europe, women can almost be said to be vegetarians. They don't like to eat meat, not because they believe in Buddhism, nor because they are poor, but because they are afraid that eating meat will ruin their slender figures. However, there are also many true vegetarians. Moral concepts of protecting animals, or hygienic scientific ideas constitute their motivation. There are always several vegetarian restaurants in big cities. I have also tried it in Germany: vegetarian dishes are more expensive than meat dishes, and the taste is not as good as that of China; but cold dishes made of red and white radish shreds, chrysanthemum-like golden bamboo shoots, and emerald green lettuce, are particularly exquisite in carving and particularly bright in color, like a work of art, making people reluctant to put them in their mouths.

There is a monastic socialist group in Europe based on the moral philosophy of Nelson (a modern German philosopher). Vegetarianism, like peace, is its main tenet. One of our friends, Ms. A, belongs to this group. Sometimes when we gather together to make Chinese food, eating large glasses of wine and large pieces of meat, she would cook some tomatoes or eggs for herself to eat. We felt that she was a bit of a killjoy, and heated debates often broke out. She solemnly stated the profound meaning of eating vegetarian, and two or three gossipy boyfriends deliberately held opposing views, bringing out all possible arguments: A proved from the philosophical and biological point of view that plants and animals are equally important, B sophistically said that no matter how vegetarians abstain from killing, they always swallow countless microorganisms in a day, and C further explained from a sociological point of view that eating meat is an important key to human evolution, but no matter how eloquently we spoke, the argumentative Ms. A still insisted on her reasons, and sometimes when she got anxious, she said with a red face.

"You are sophistical, I won't argue with you."

When I was about to return to China, Ms. A specially ran from the outer city to Berlin to see us. In order to fulfill the duties of a host, we all ate vegetarian food, and even cooked the dishes ourselves. Once I wanted to make a spicy stir-fried shredded cabbage. In order to save effort, I used a toothed plane to grate the shreds. Who knew that the plane was too fast, and I accidentally cut my finger, taking off a piece of skin and flesh, and bleeding several drops. Mr. B, who was cooking with me, laughed at me for being useless, and then continued to grate. Who knew that he would also lose some flesh and blood as soon as he started. Although we washed the shredded cabbage carefully, we believed that there would always be some of our flesh and blood mixed in it.

"Eating vegetarian this time has turned into eating human flesh!" Mr. B chuckled.

This socialist group also runs a family-like small school in the countryside not far from Berlin, with food and lodging all in the school. A French friend of Mr. B had a six-year-old daughter, who was also studying there. After Hitler came to power, this group and its affiliated school became illegal and were dissolved. Entrusted by his friend, Mr. B took her daughter to Paris. I met this girl at Mr. B's house. Although she was as excited as other children when she saw cocoa candies and Western pastries, when we persuaded her to eat a slice of ham, she would stubbornly argue about the great principles of vegetarianism. We had already learned her arguments from Ms. A, and there was not much difference. Later, when she became more familiar with us, even others eating meat would elicit a small sermon from her.

"Annoying vegetarian preacher!" Mr. B said with a smile when he couldn't stand it anymore.

Now these friends have scattered, and I don't know where Ms. A has gone. Speaking of eating vegetarian, I can't help but bitterly remember them.

Historical Tales of Friendship 2

— Ling Jing

It is commonly said that Guan Zhong and Bao Shuya are the standard for friends who value faith and righteousness, but this may not be entirely accurate. According to the "Biography of Guan Zhong" in the "Records of the Grand Historian," Guan Zhong fully demonstrated that he was a petty man who only knew how to benefit himself, while Bao Shuya was a person of faith and righteousness who was "good enough as a friend." In general, it is relatively easy to simply talk about "faith" in friendship, but it is quite difficult to be able to fulfill "righteousness." Chinese people have always valued family concepts, especially the parent-child relationship, which is regarded as particularly important. Therefore, among the five relationships, the parent-child relationship ranks second, only one level lower than the ruler-subject relationship. However, the friend relationship ranks last, much less important than the sibling and spouse relationships. The "Book of Rites" says: "When parents are alive, one should not pledge to die for a friend." Because one has parents and pledges oneself to others, it is to forget one's parents. Therefore, if parents are still alive, a child cannot avenge his friend. It can be seen that it is not easy to achieve the "righteousness" between friends in China. However, although this is said, it is not necessarily true that everyone can follow the teachings of the sages. The "Twenty-Four Histories" are full of examples of valuing righteousness. The "Biography of Wu Fan" in the "Records of Wu" in the "Records of the Three Kingdoms" says:

"Fan and Wei Teng were from the same town and had a good relationship. Teng once committed a crime, and Quan was angry and strict, saying that anyone who dared to admonish would die. Fan said to Teng: "I will die with you!" Teng said: "Dying is useless, what is the use of dying?" Fan said: "How can I consider this and sit and watch you?" So he shaved his head and went to the gate, asking the guards to report it. The guards did not dare to report it, saying: "It will surely lead to death, I dare not report it." Fan said: "Do you have a son?" The guards said: "Yes." Fan said: "If I let your son die for Wu Fan, your son will belong to me."

The guards said: "Yes." So he pushed open the door and entered. Before he finished speaking, Quan was furious and wanted to throw a halberd at him. Fan quickly ran out, and Fan took the opportunity to rush in, kowtowing and shedding blood, speaking and weeping at the same time. After a long time, Quan's anger subsided and he spared Teng. When Teng saw Fan, he thanked him and said: "My parents could give birth to me and raise me, but they could not save me from death. For a man to know each other, having you is enough, what need is there for more?"

Wu Fan's saving of Wei Teng was entirely for the "righteousness" of friendship, which moved Wei Teng to say something quite "rebellious." If the Duke of Zhou and Confucius were in Wei Teng's situation that day, they would probably overturn their own teachings that they considered to be great principles. However, we cannot blindly use the word "righteousness." The kind of righteousness of the Jianghu gangs is not worthy of our emulation. We should add a sense of right and wrong to private feelings. Wu Fan's sacrifice to save Wei Teng was because Wei Teng was indeed a gentleman with a rigid nature and did not act in a compromising manner. If Wei Teng was a despicable villain who coveted power and misled the country, then Wu Fan's actions would probably not be understood and would not be recorded in history. The importance of being a man lies in the sense of right and wrong. If you can grasp this key point, at least you can be considered to have done half of being a man. If you further "sacrifice yourself for righteousness," you will naturally become a great hero without a doubt. Wu Fan is one, and Wang Hui's actions in the Song Dynasty were even more unrestrained. The "Biography of Zou Hao" in the "History of the Song Dynasty" says:

"Wang Hui, whose courtesy name was Jing Shen, was from Xianyou. He was a good friend of Zou Hao. When Empress Liu was established, Hao was about to discuss it and secretly told Hui. Hui said: "Is there anything greater than this matter? Although you have parents, transferring filial piety to loyalty is also the long-cherished wish of the old lady." Hao moved south, and no one cared for him. Hui collected money from his friends to prepare for his journey, and went back and forth to manage it, personally comforting his mother. The guards reported it, and he was arrested and sent to prison. Everyone was afraid for him, but Hui remained calm. The censor questioned him, and he replied: "I did participate in the discussion, I dare not deceive." Then he recited the two thousand words of Hao's memorial. When the prison report was submitted, his name was removed and he was dismissed. He immediately walked out of the capital gate. After walking dozens of miles, his son caught up and asked about family matters, and he answered again..."

Like Wang Hui's actions, although his starting point was still the word "righteousness," it was too unrestrained after all, because even if he did not admit to conspiring, it would not necessarily hinder Zou Hao, and admitting it would still not reduce Zou Hao's crime. However, everyone has their own personality, and it is impossible to force people to do things they don't want to do. His kind of ancient style is quite worthy of reflection in today's frivolous and servile society. Tao Zongyi of the Ming Dynasty recorded a story in his "辍耕录," which is also close to a righteous act, but is not the same as the behavior of the two people mentioned above, but is somewhat "close to ostentation":

"In Hangzhou's subordinate county, there was a wealthy family that relied on wealth and power to abuse good people. The county officials were corrupt and no one dared to do anything. The people could not bear it and ran to the constitutional government to sue. The wealthy family fled and hid. The constitutional envoy was angry and ordered the authorities to severely punish them, showing the crimes and rewards, posting them on the main roads, and going to each house to post announcements: Those who hide them will be implicated! Those who capture them will be rewarded with ten thousand strings of cash. His friend, Wang Yishan, a scholar by profession, lived in the No. 1 building in the lake and mountains. He hid him secretly and did not reveal him for a month. A neighbor found out and planned to seek the reward money, reporting it to the official. The official searched and found him, and arrested and imprisoned Wang together. When he saw the constitutional envoy, the envoy asked: "Do you know what crime he committed?" Wang said: "I know." "Have you heard of the laws of the country?" He said: "I know." "Have you seen the announcement of crimes and rewards?" He said: "I have seen it." "Why don't you seek profit and avoid harm?" He said: "When a friend is in trouble and comes to me for help, taking advantage of his danger to sell him out is not allowed by the teachings of morality. I sincerely cannot bear to do it. If the matter is discovered and I am implicated, I am willing to do so." The envoy was startled and said: "The gentleman said, 'Do not seek to avoid danger.' This person practices it. He is truly a righteous man. If I add to his crime, it is because my government is harsh and my punishment is excessive. How can the people be encouraged?" So he released him..."

Tao Zongyi and this constitutional envoy both praised Wang Yishan's virtue of righteousness, perhaps because Tu Yishan was a Confucian wearing a square scarf. In fact, they were both fooled by this gentleman with a square scarf. Who knows if his hiding of the wealthy family was not for the sake of "relying on good fortune" in the future? Relying only on a few clichés of a corrupt scholar, he was allowed to escape the law and was full of the reputation of "righteous man." I think this constitutional envoy must also be a fame-seeker. There is a story in "Laughing Zen Records": "Ju Yi asked Xue Feng to ask the master to indicate the Buddhist Dharma. Feng said: "What are you talking about? Two friends, A and B, were usually very close. One day, A happened to be ill and could not bear the pain. B came to ask and said: Brother, what is your illness? What do you need? I can do it all. A said: I am suffering from the disease of money, and I only need two or three cymbals to recover. B immediately pretended not to hear and swallowed and said: What did you say? Song said: Gold is as precious as the Buddha Dharma, the Buddha Dharma is as precious as gold. When you look for it, you cannot get it. I have already reassured you." Wang Yishan is probably one of the A and B types."

A Couple (1)

— Bai Chen

Tram number three was heading south from Carter Road. It stopped at the New Zhabei Bridge. It was three o'clock after lunch, and there were quite a few people getting on the tram. Eight out of ten of the third-class passengers by the entrance of the trailer were people in short gowns. However, those squeezed by the small third-class entrance were people in long gowns, and there were even a few people in suits. At the first-class entrance, there was no one—no, while people were crowding into the small third-class entrance, two passengers ran to the first-class entrance. In front was a man with a fair and clean face, and behind was a woman with light lipstick on her lips.

There was no one in first class. The man just ran straight in. The woman entered and tilted her backside to sit down. With a "whoosh," the man pulled open the glass door and squeezed into the third-class carriage. The woman looked back and followed him in.

The man spread his buttocks and opened his legs, claiming two seats to sit down. A friend who came in from the small third-class entrance rolled his eyes at him. The woman had already picked it up: The man folded his legs, and the woman sat down. She looked around and lowered her head to ask the man: "Third class?"

The man glared at her and nodded.

The tram rattled past a station.

"Soy Sauce Lane!"

The ticket seller came over, weighing the coins in his hand, and circled them in front of everyone's faces.

"Do you have any?" He asked.

The man didn't make a sound.

The Birthday of Dizang

— Tang Xiru

By evening, the children living together were chattering like birds returning to their nests, fighting over the sweet potatoes. They stuck burning incense sticks all over the sweet potatoes, making them look like hedgehogs. Then they strung them with thread and held them in their hands or hung them in the hall. They watched these spiky hedgehogs of fire, jumping and shouting with joy, even though the thick smoke stung their eyes so much they couldn't open them.

Seeing this peculiar toy, it was like suddenly recalling something long forgotten, remembering that today is the thirtieth day of the seventh month in the lunar calendar, the birthday of Dizang Wang (Earth Store Bodhisattva).

Hearing the fellow residents say that by nightfall, the streets would be full of large and small incense balls, some made of pumpkins, some of sweet potatoes, and many made of very large rice gourds, along the steps of each house, forming a long row of incense sticks. Moreover, people closed their doors early, so going for a stroll on the street tonight would have a different flavor.

Being urged by the fellow residents, I hadn't planned to go out that night, but after finishing dinner, I wanted to go out and take a look.

Stepping onto the dark long street, there were groups of wild children running, shouting, and laughing. Before my eyes were patterns formed by small dots of fire, with thick smoke. Even in such a dark night, you could see how furiously it was spewing. The scent of incense sticks, which was not very pleasant to begin with, was now so excessively strong that it was unbearable, as if it were pickling the brain.

I forced myself to walk for a few dozen houses, but in the end, I couldn't force myself any longer. With a feeling of grievance, I quickly ran back.

As I stepped into the doorway of my residence, I ran into one of the fellow residents. He greeted me with a smile:

"Not bad, right? That...!"

I felt that his smile had a hint of mockery.

"There are too many incense sticks lit, it's too strong and unbearable!" I said.

"Ah! It's the birthday of Dizang!" The fellow resident was a little surprised.

"And it's just lighting incense, it's too monotonous. Why not add some candles?"

"No way! Today is the birthday of Dizang!" He said again, surprised. "He's going to pass by here tonight!"

I wanted to say that lighting a few more candles and lighting a few less incense sticks, to light up a section of the road for him, so that he would sneeze a few less times, wouldn't Dizang Wang be even more welcome? But when I saw his serious face, I pretended to understand everything and "uh"ed a few times. The road came in.

A few days later, I learned the whole story from others.

Because of his great power and high position, Dizang Wang does not easily open his eyes. Perhaps it is because he does not easily open his eyes? If he saw so much sin and so much evil of mankind, he would not like it and would bring disasters to mankind, such as earthquakes and plagues. Wouldn't this destroy mankind in a few strokes? No, people have ways to deal with it. That is, when this Bodhisattva goes on patrol or opens his eyes, nominally they are welcoming him or paying respect to him, but in reality, they are using this thick smoke to prevent him from looking directly or staying for a while. This method can be said to be the same as bribing the Kitchen God when bribing heaven.

Mankind has not yet been exterminated. We seem to owe it to ourselves for being able to come up with such a clever and win-win method of coping.

I have seen the statue of Dizang Wang in the temple. Solemn! Great! But his eyes are closed. I always feel that his closed eyelids were forced to be closed by us humans, especially by those with deep sins.

And I now also believe that he is used to this kind of life, and he will be willing to close his eyes even on the one day that mankind specifically allows him to open his eyes and go on patrol, after being deceived countless times.

Mother

— Nan Yun

Let the sound of the scattered rain knock back the heart of the shattered wanderer!

No, the wanderer's heart was shattered long ago – that was eight years ago when the waves of the era rose.

At that time, I was very young. What did a sixteen- or seventeen-year-old girl understand? However, in order to study, I simply changed my life. I remember: After I began to put down the pen that was learning from Bing Xin to write poems praising my mother, I eliminated my idle worries, strengthened myself, yearned for light, and went forward fearlessly.

Who knew that in this way, I began my life of drifting and wandering.

I love my mother, but I gave her sorrow. None of the hopes that all mothers of the old century placed on their daughters did I give her. What I gave her was:

The ridicule of relatives! The slander of feudal society! …

I also remember her crying in front of me. At first I was sad, then I was indignant! Mother, why can't you be a mother of all humanity!

Although I knew that it was for my own pure, brave, and youthful innocence that I accepted the misfortunes of the world. But to reverse this misfortune, it was clear that I had to break away from everything and embark on the road of my own century.

Here, I repeatedly left my beloved mother with a body full of wounds.

For five years, I have traveled north and south, tasting the bitter wine of the era. Every time I saw an old man with white hair, I couldn't help but think of my mother at home.

Mother! I don't know what the beauty of your white hair has become? I can only guess during the day, and search in my dreams, dragging a tired body, and coming to this rainy and windy foreign land again.

The exotic atmosphere cannot move my heart. Those who are used to wandering have long forgotten the difference between the ends of the earth and their hometown. Only when I think of my mother, I am afraid to listen to the low hum of the wind and the sob of the rain!

Commercial News

New High Price for Gold Speculation: 1152 Yuan

Situation Stable Before Special Tax Increase on Both Parties, Exchange Market Tense, Resulting in a Sharp Rise of 18.5 Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market was initially stable in the morning session due to news of the exchange increasing special tax on sellers. However, rumors about "Fuxing" (a company or entity) emerged in the afternoon, leading to overwhelming buying interest and pushing the price to a new peak of 1152 yuan. Initial market conditions were calm, with overseas silver markets showing a slight decline in England and stability in America. The forward silver price in Montreux remained unchanged or slightly decreased. Exchange rates were generally positive, and the London gold price remained stable. Market sentiment was peaceful. The exchange then issued a notice stating that sellers must also pay a special deposit of 50 yuan per bar, and that guaranteed shares under brand names, using only the deposit, should not exceed 70 bars. This boosted general confidence. Pre-market trading opened, immediately rising to 23-24 yuan, with strong buying demand. It further rose to over 30 yuan. Several major firms sold, gradually retreating to within 20 yuan. The morning session opened lower, gradually declining due to heavy selling pressure, but maintained a level after the drop. The Central Bank's exchange rate announcement showed a decrease in both British and American rates, while the customs gold unit rose by one-third of a cent. The standard gold price was listed at 1042.8 yuan. Market sentiment remained steady, gradually rising to above 20 yuan. Banks initially supported the shilling, temporarily strengthening it, but then took advantage of the high prices to release US dollars, anticipating the HSBC exchange rate. The British rate remained flat, while the American rate rose by 0.0625. Soon after, it dropped back to within 20 yuan. Sassoon and Shanghai firms heavily sold shillings, hardening the domestic market and triggering active selling. It gradually declined again, but banks and the Sanwa Bank bought in at lower prices, maintaining a stable level. It gradually recovered to above 20 yuan. The forecast for Indian silver was a drop of six annas. The situation remained stable at noon. Later, a Reuters news report about the Central Bank of Manchuria ordering the centralization of silver reserves stirred the market. The market immediately stabilized upon opening. Cantonese merchants bought US dollars, increasing buying interest and breaking through the 30 yuan barrier. Reasons for Adding Water to Head Money to Raise Prices

Domestic Market Interest Rates Open at 5.5 Yuan

Everyone knows the current market is in distress. The reporters need not to explain this. However, in the past few days, adding water to head money has continued to increase, raising prices. The reason is nothing more than the fact that large foreign loan payments are being made, and head money is gradually becoming unsustainable. Now, with foreign exchange settlement and expenditure of difference money, and various payments for imported goods, a huge amount must be paid out at the end of the month, so head money is particularly tight. Adding water to head money is therefore expensive due to the shortage. In a few days, it has risen from 0.7-0.8 cents to 0.2 yuan. As for foreign exchange loans, due to credit concerns, no one dares to accept the loan, and even if they do, no one is willing to grant it. Therefore, there is very little competition in the market, and the result is no significant change. Most of the various long-term loans that have come due have been completed. There are still many loans that have not come due and will gradually come due soon, totaling no less than 30 million. They must be sorted out in these three days. Yesterday, the amount due at banks was several hundred thousand, and the amount due for credit loans at Qianzhuang was 5-600,000, and pledge loans were more than 1.5 million, with a total of 5-6 million. Most of them were transferred to accounts. In addition, many long-term deposits have been negotiated and fixed, and the interest rate must be based on domestic market interest rates. However, the domestic market interest rate on the 27th had already opened at 5.5 yuan, equivalent to the previous period. This time, most depositors want an additional 0.5 or 1 yuan based on the domestic market interest rate. It is reported that over 1 million agreed to add 0.5 yuan and 1 yuan. The remaining interest rates are fixed based on the domestic market price. In addition, there are some scattered long-term deposits, which have come due for account transfers and repayments, totaling approximately 2-300,000. These are personal loans from various shops in the concession, so they have not been added to the overall market price.

Silver Movements in the London Market: China Sells, America Buys

In the London silver market in the past month (September 30 to October 28), America was a major buyer, China was a major seller, and India had both buying and selling. In the first half of the month, it was buying, and in the second half of the month, it was selling. China, due to fears of inflation and the skyrocketing gold price, experienced even more capital flight. Those with funds rushed to buy foreign exchange. Banks also promoted "foreign currency deposits." The strong buying of foreign exchange inevitably led to the selling of silver. It is said that China had a silver trade surplus of 7 million yuan in previous quarters, so selling is not a problem. However, the amount of silver sold this time is currently unknown, so we cannot be too optimistic. In short, silver prices are fluctuating, and there is no hope for market recovery.

Therefore, most speculative longs could not help but feel uneasy, and prices opened down by 5 to 6 fen. Later, because the decline in the flour market was very sharp, prices fell even more. From November to January, prices fell by 7 to 8 fen. The February contract fell the most sharply, falling by 1 jiao 3 fen. Until the afternoon, the market was initially stable, but then the gold market soared, and flour also rebounded, causing speculative buying to surge again. The price increases for each month varied slightly due to different trading volumes. For example, the rebound in the December contract even exceeded the morning decline, while the remaining contracts rebounded by 6 to 7 fen to nearly a jiao, similar to the previous day. Spot wheat prices have eased slightly, and customers have not tightened up. Sales of each grade opened, falling by about 5 to 6 fen. Shandong wheat opened at 4 yuan 6 jiao 4 fen, and Yaowan Gaoyou wheat opened at 4 yuan 6 jiao, totaling 4,000 bales. It is said that Shanfu has just opened a new office. In addition, the 800 yuan special certificate for grain delivery has been cancelled. From yesterday onwards, the margin for wheat and soybean bidding is uniformly 400 yuan, and the margin for oil cakes is uniformly 280 yuan. After the market stabilizes, the old system will be restored.
